### `row_0630`
> The key to understanding how a group of 50 people can have over a 90% chance of sharing a birthday lies in the number of possible comparisons between individuals. [alce::row_0630::p54]
> When you add people to a group, the number of comparisons grows rapidly—Person A can be compared with 49 others, Person B with 48 others (excluding the already-counted comparison with A), Person C with 47 others, and so on, creating many opportunities for a match. [alce::row_0630::p54]
> With 50 people in a group, there is a 97% chance that at least two people will share the same birthday. [alce::row_0630::p60]
> This probability exceeds 90% because the combinatorial nature of the problem means that even though any single person has only a 1 in 365.242 chance of matching another specific person's birthday, the sheer number of possible pairwise comparisons makes a match highly likely. [alce::row_0630::p54]

Cited: alce::row_0630::p54, alce::row_0630::p60

### `row_0641`
> # What Happens to Insects in Winter and How They Repopulate

In cold climates, insects do not all die off uniformly; instead, they employ various survival strategies. [alce::row_0641::p1]
> Insects have a variety of methods for surviving the coldness of winter, with migration being one strategy for escaping killing temperatures. [alce::row_0641::p74]
> In cold weather, insects and mites produce a type of anti-freeze in their bodies or locate in overwintering sites that do not actually freeze. [alce::row_0641::p74]
> These pests are rarely killed by the extremes of cold in their normal range unless a rare, super cold period is experienced.

Regarding rapid repopulation once temperatures warm, the sources indicate that insects can reproduce quickly during the warm season. [alce::row_0641::p41]
> The survival of termites in cold climates depends on their ability to repopulate during the warm season. [alce::row_0641::p10]
> As the planet warms, insect species can spread into more areas and stay more active during the year, allowing them more time to reproduce.

### `row_0645`
> Based on the provided sources, I can offer the following explanation:

Gas flaring occurs because gases cannot easily be captured and put to productive use. [alce::row_0645::p4]
> Additionally, some flaring is considered necessary for safety reasons, as it serves as a safety-valve in high pressure systems. [alce::row_0645::p4]

### `row_0646`
> In winter, it is still cold even when the sun is out and there are no clouds because of how the sun's rays strike the Earth. [alce::row_0646::p37]
> The Earth's rotational axis is tilted 23.5° relative to the Sun, which means that during winter in the Northern Hemisphere, the region is pointed slightly away from the Sun. [alce::row_0646::p37]
> This angle causes sunlight to hit the ground at a lower angle in winter than in summer, which spreads out the energy coming from the Sun. [alce::row_0646::p37]
> In summer, it is hot because the sun's rays strike the Earth at a higher angle, concentrating the solar energy rather than spreading it out. [alce::row_0646::p37]
> The difference in the angle at which the sun's rays hit the ground between winter and summer is the key reason for the temperature difference, not the presence or absence of clouds. [alce::row_0646::p37]

Cited: alce::row_0646::p37

### `row_0691`
> # Entropy in Thermodynamics and Everyday Life

Entropy is a concept used to describe configurations of nature's substance and enables conceptual formulations about the behaviors of thermodynamic systems. [alce::row_0691::p4]
> It is closely related to the number of microscopic configurations that are consistent with the macroscopic quantities that characterize a system, such as its volume, pressure, and temperature. [alce::row_0691::p0]
> In thermodynamics, entropy can be related to internal energy, pressure, volume, temperature, chemical potential, and other thermodynamic quantities through thermodynamic identities. [alce::row_0691::p82]
> The second law of thermodynamics states that entropy in an isolated system increases during all spontaneous chemical and physical processes. [alce::row_0691::p35]
> Regarding everyday life relevance, the concept of "irreversibility" is central to understanding entropy, and everyone has an intuitive understanding of irreversibility from observing everyday events. [alce::row_0691::p0]
> A practical everyday example is ice melting, which demonstrates entropy increasing. [alce::row_0691::p0]
> Additionally, when you buy a new set of Legos, the entropy of the set is at its highest before you build the model because at that point those Legos could be used to create many different configurations. [alce::row_0691::p82]

Cited: alce::row_0691::p0, alce::row_0691::p35, alce::row_0691::p4, alce::row_0691::p82

### `row_0695`
> # Brain Pulses: What They Mean and Tracking Them

**What Brain Pulses Mean:**

Electrical pulses carry signals along the branches of neurons. [alce::row_0695::p73]
> Every experience you have corresponds to its own unique pattern of electrical activity in the nervous system and brain. [alce::row_0695::p73]
> Forty times a second an electrical pulse is sent across the brain, and some neuroscientists currently believe that this pulse regulates the neural firings in the brain and thus many of the body's rhythms. [alce::row_0695::p22]
> Additionally, sensory processing echoes and reverberates with these pulses and gives us a sense of time passing. [alce::row_0695::p8]
> **Can We Track Our Own:**

Yes, we currently have the power to detect brainwaves and track electrical pulses within the neurons in our brains. [alce::row_0695::p0]
> In the future, it is expected that fitness trackers, smart watches, or Bluetooth headphones will start tracking our cognitive activity and reading our pulses for signs of electrical brain activity. [alce::row_0695::p1]

> Roof venting does not make the fire worse by adding oxygen. Instead, it serves several critical firefighting purposes.

When firefighters vent the roof by cutting holes, dangerous gases and dark smoke escape from the building. [alce::row_0730::p7]

> Another benefit is that it reduces the possibilities of backdraft and flashover, which are dangerous explosions. [alce::row_0730::p18]
> Finally, venting allows firefighters to access the attic and stop the fire from spreading through it, since the attic is one of the fastest avenues through which fires spread. [alce::row_0730::p18]

### `row_0757`
> Acetaminophen is bad for your liver because when the drug is metabolized in the liver, it releases a toxic substance called NAPQI (N-acetyl-p-benzoquinoneimine). [alce::row_0757::p35]
> This NAPQI can accumulate in the liver, and the liver won't be able to process it effectively, causing NAPQI to start damaging liver cells. [alce::row_0757::p35]

### `row_0759`
> # How Computer Viruses and Malware Work

Viruses are programs that copy themselves and infect a computer, spreading from one computer to another, similar to how biological viruses work. [alce::row_0759::p62]
> A virus is specifically a type of malware that is capable of self-replicating once it enters the computer. [alce::row_0759::p19]
> Trojans are a different type of malware—they are applications that look normal but contain hidden malicious code. [alce::row_0759::p62]
> Malware is a broader term that encompasses viruses, trojans, adware, spyware, ransomware, and other types of malicious software, with each type operating differently. [alce::row_0759::p19]
> Viruses typically arrive on your computer hidden inside another program, often delivered by email. [alce::row_0759::p57]
> # What Makes Them Harmful

Malware is created to do harm, and the primary objective is nearly always to make money in various ways. [alce::row_0759::p4]
> When attacking businesses, cyberattackers are typically after clients' information, which gives them the chance to install malware on their computers or gain access to bank accounts if financial information has been improperly stored. [alce::row_0759::p4]
> Additionally, malware can see what you're doing and, in some cases, steal personal information or passwords.
> Malware can also take up a lot of disk space, which consumes valuable storage capacity. [alce::row_0759::p57]

Cited: alce::row_0759::p19, alce::row_0759::p4, alce::row_0759::p57, alce::row_0759::p62

### `row_0762`
> # Difference Between Value, Price, and Cost

**Price** is the amount of money asked for or the number on the price tag informing customers how much something costs. [alce::row_0762::p28]
> It represents what you pay for a given product or service. [alce::row_0762::p10]
> **Cost** is the amount actually paid for something. [alce::row_0762::p28]
> It can also refer to the historical construction cost of improvements plus the land, or the theoretical replacement cost to re-establish an asset. [alce::row_0762::p1]
> **Value** is what any given product or service is worth, or the benefit derived from an action. [alce::row_0762::p10]
> Unlike price and cost, value is always justifiable. [alce::row_0762::p28]
> The key distinction is that although these three terms are sometimes used interchangeably, they are not synonymous. [alce::row_0762::p28]
> A property's value can be different from both the price that a willing buyer and seller agree upon and the actual cost. [alce::row_0762::p1]

Cited: alce::row_0762::p1, alce::row_0762::p10, alce::row_0762::p28

### `row_0763`
> # How Car Speedometers and Tachometers Work

## Speedometer

The speedometer is the most prominent gauge in your car's dashboard instrument cluster. [alce::row_0763::p5]
> Its job is to indicate the speed of your car in miles per hour, kilometers per hour, or both. [alce::row_0763::p5]
> Even in late-model cars, the speedometer is an analog device that uses a mechanical system. [alce::row_0763::p5]
> Both modern digital displays and decades-old manual needle meters fundamentally rely on information from the tachometer-shaft, a technology that is well over half a century old and remains in use because of its accuracy and durability. [alce::row_0763::p4]
> ## Tachometer

The tachometer, or rev counter, is an instrument for measuring the speed of an engine's rotation. [alce::row_0763::p7]
> Unlike the speedometer, the tachometer is not a legal requirement. [alce::row_0763::p7]
> In modern cars, the tachometer works using a device that consists of a magnet wrapped with wire located very near a saw-toothed wheel that spins as the engine turns. [alce::row_0763::p56]
> This device is essentially an electric generator, where the toothed wheel is made of pure iron so that its teeth can become temporarily magnetized while they are close to the permanent magnet. [alce::row_0763::p56]

> # Why We Itch and What Happens in Your Skin

**General causes of itching:**
Itching can be caused by many different things, including allergies, insect bites, dry skin, and illness. [alce::row_0786::p90]
> **How itching begins:**
When something on or in the skin triggers an event in the brain, this instinctively causes you to scratch. [alce::row_0786::p24]
> The itch reflex is a protective response developed to help animals remove parasites from their skin. [alce::row_0786::p90]
> **Random itches specifically:**
Nobody really knows why spontaneous itches occur. [alce::row_0786::p4]
> However, random itches are related to several phenomena of the central nervous system, and one factor in their cause is sensory filtering, which occurs both in the spinal cord and the brain and is so comprehensive that very little sensory information actually gets projected to consciousness. [alce::row_0786::p50]
> Additionally, sometimes itching arises from neurological or psychiatric causes with no strictly external stimulus at all. [alce::row_0786::p24]
> **What's happening in your skin when not scratching:**
When you experience an itch, skin receptors are stimulated, which sends a signal to the brain. [alce::row_0786::p41]
> The major neuronal pathway for itch in the central nervous system is not fully understood. [alce::row_0786::p50]

### `row_0803`

### `row_0804`
> GPS receivers calculate their deviation from true time by monitoring multiple satellites and solving equations. [alce::row_0804::p1]
> At a minimum, four satellites must be in view of the receiver for it to compute four unknown quantities: three position coordinates and clock deviation from satellite time. [alce::row_0804::p3]
> The calculation process relies on the time delay between when each satellite sends a signal and when the receiver collects it; since radio waves travel at a constant speed, this time delay is proportional to the distance from the satellite to the receiver. [alce::row_0804::p4]
> By time-aligning a receiver-generated version with the receiver-measured version of the pseudorandom code broadcast by each satellite, the receiver can determine the time of arrival of a defined point in the code sequence.

Cited: alce::row_0804::p1, alce::row_0804::p3, alce::row_0804::p4

### `row_0853`
> # How and Why Fireflies Glow

**How Fireflies Glow:**

A firefly glows through a process called bioluminescence. [alce::row_0853::p7]
> The glow originates from the lower part of their abdomen in a structure called a "lantern." [alce::row_0853::p41]
> Light is produced by a small layer of cells called photocytes, and this light is reflected off several layers of reflective cells to emit a greenish-yellow glow. [alce::row_0853::p41]
> Specifically, a firefly inhales oxygen, which reacts with a chemical called luciferin in its light-emitting organ to produce light. [alce::row_0853::p12]
> The light produced is "cold light," meaning it generates almost no heat and is 100% efficient. [alce::row_0853::p72]
> **Why Fireflies Glow:**

Fireflies glow for multiple reasons that vary by species and life stage. [alce::row_0853::p74]
> Firefly larvae use their bioluminescent flashes to communicate distaste. [alce::row_0853::p74]
> Adult fireflies glow in order to identify members of their own species as well as to communicate during courtship. [alce::row_0853::p74]
> Additionally, the lights are used for defense. [alce::row_0853::p72]

Cited: alce::row_0853::p12, alce::row_0853::p41, alce::row_0853::p7, alce::row_0853::p72, alce::row_0853::p74

A game engine is a framework specifically targeted to make games, and it usually includes graphics, input handling, and other auxiliary APIs. [alce::row_0858::p67]
> Game engines are more specialized than general frameworks and typically come with authoring tools like model editors or importers. [alce::row_0858::p67]

When people remake games using the Unreal Engine, they gain access to tools that make game development easier and more accessible. [alce::row_0858::p68]
> The Unreal Engine is known for its large customizability and multiple platform capabilities, allowing developers to create HD AAA games more easily. [alce::row_0858::p24]

### `row_0888`

> Because your actual body temperature is now below this newly elevated thermostat setting, your body perceives itself as being cold even though your temperature is actually high. [alce::row_0888::p21]
> Your body then produces chills—which are muscle contractions that consume energy and generate heat—in an attempt to raise your actual temperature up to match the new thermostat setting. [alce::row_0888::p21]
> This feeling of cold and the urge to cover up is therefore beneficial because it drives your body to generate the higher temperature needed to fight the infection. [alce::row_0888::p21]
> However, bundling up with blankets when you have a fever can actually increase your body temperature further, which won't help you feel better.
> Instead, you should dress lightly to help your body cool down. [alce::row_0888::p27]

> # Different Types of Web Hosting

There are primarily six main types of web hosting: free, shared, dedicated, collocated, VPS, and reseller. [alce::row_0911::p4]
> The differences between these types are primarily based on the infrastructure that is used and the manner in which each web hosting account of all clients is managed by the host. [alce::row_0911::p4]
> **Shared Hosting** is the most basic and most affordable type of web hosting, where different websites are hosted on a single physical web server. [alce::row_0911::p6]
> Shared web hosting is the most popular form of hosting. [alce::row_0911::p3]
> **Dedicated Hosting** is another common type available for businesses. [alce::row_0911::p2]
> **Free Web Hosting** is one of the available options. [alce::row_0911::p2]
> **Collocated Hosting** is also among the most common types of web hosts. [alce::row_0911::p2]
> **VPS Hosting** is another type of web hosting that companies provide. [alce::row_0911::p6]
> **Cloud Hosting** and **E-commerce Hosting** are additional types of web hosting, though they are classified differently as they can be offered as free, shared, dedicated, collocated, VPS, or reseller hosting accounts. [alce::row_0911::p4]
> There are also specialized hosting types such as 1-Click WordPress Hosting, CMS Hosting (Drupal & Joomla), and Reseller Hosting. [alce::row_0911::p6]

### `row_0928`
> # The Difference Between Rugby Union and Rugby League (ELI5)

Rugby Union and Rugby League are two different versions of rugby that split apart a long time ago. [alce::row_0928::p2]
> **Number of Players:** Rugby Union has 15 players on the field, while Rugby League has only 13 players. [alce::row_0928::p1]
> **Tackle Rule:** In Rugby League, you only get six tackles before you have to give the ball to the other team, but Rugby Union doesn't have this rule. [alce::row_0928::p1]
> **What Happens When the Ball Goes Out:** When the ball goes out of play in League, there's a scrum, but in Union there's a line-out instead. [alce::row_0928::p4]
> **How Plays Restart:** League uses something called a "play-the-ball restart," while Union uses "mauls" and "rucks." [alce::row_0928::p4]
> **Substitutions:** Rugby League allows 10 substitutions, while Rugby Union allows only 8. [alce::row_0928::p15]

Cited: alce::row_0928::p1, alce::row_0928::p15, alce::row_0928::p2, alce::row_0928::p4

### `row_0933`
> The premise of your question contains an inaccuracy that the sources address.

In at-will employment relationships, neither employees nor employers are legally required to provide notice before terminating employment. [alce::row_0933::p12]
> Employers may terminate employees at any time without notice, and employees may quit suddenly without providing notice. [alce::row_0933::p1]
> However, there is a practical difference in expectations. Employers want employees to give two weeks' notice because it helps them prepare for the departure by hiring a replacement and taking other steps to continue business with minimal disruption. [alce::row_0933::p0]
> Although giving two weeks' notice is customary and considered good etiquette or common courtesy on the part of employees, it is not legally required. [alce::row_0933::p1]
> The asymmetry you've identified is not based on legal requirements, but rather on practical business needs and social convention that favor advance notice from departing employees.

### `row_0938`
> The Austrian School of Economics is a tradition of economic thought founded by Carl Menger in the last third of the nineteenth century. [alce::row_0938::p33]
> It is a heterodox school of economic thought based on methodological individualism—the concept that social phenomena result from the motivations and actions of individuals. [alce::row_0938::p45]
> The school originated in late-nineteenth and early-twentieth century Vienna with the work of Carl Menger, Eugen Böhm von Bawerk, Friedrich von Wieser and others. [alce::row_0938::p45]
> Prominent authors in this tradition include Ludwig von Mises, Friedrich Hayek, Ludwig Lachmann, Murray N. Rothbard and Jesús Huerta de Soto. [alce::row_0938::p33]
> The most remarkable characteristic of the Austrian School is its emphasis on a causal-realistic approach based on the concept of methodological individualism. [alce::row_0938::p33]
> A key aspect of Austrian economic thought is Menger's application of the concept of intentionality to economic value, considering that economic value derives from a judgment that expresses a preference. [alce::row_0938::p33]

Cited: alce::row_0938::p33, alce::row_0938::p45

### `row_0955`
> Countries are widely known by names that differ from their native names because these are called exonyms—names by which one people or group refers to another, and by which the group so named does not refer to itself. [alce::row_0955::p2]
> The English word "Japan" is an exonym, while the Japanese people actually call their country "Nippon" or "Nihon." [alce::row_0955::p2]
> This pattern occurs on an international scale with many countries; for example, Egypt is called "Al-Misr" by its own people but is known internationally as "Egypt," and similar cases exist with India (called "Bharat" natively) and Greece (called "Hellas" natively). [alce::row_0955::p29]
> The reason these exonyms persist is that countries with ancient civilizations and long histories of international contact have become known to the world by these external names, and native populations have not forced the world to adopt their own names instead. [alce::row_0955::p29]

Cited: alce::row_0955::p2, alce::row_0955::p29

### `row_0972`
> # Understanding Rastafarianism

Rastafari is an Abrahamic religion that developed in Jamaica during the 1930s. [alce::row_0972::p59]
> It is classified as both a new religious movement and a social movement. [alce::row_0972::p59]
> The core belief uniting the diverse movement is worship of Ethiopian Emperor Haile Selassie I as God incarnate, the Second Advent, or the reincarnation of Jesus. [alce::row_0972::p50]
> Rastas have faith in the divinity and/or messiahship of Haile Selassie I. [alce::row_0972::p5]
> The movement encompasses several key themes: the spiritual use of cannabis, [alce::row_0972::p50]
> resistance of oppression, and pride in African heritage. [alce::row_0972::p5]
> Rastas often claim the flag of Ethiopia as used during Haile Selassie's reign, which combines the conquering lion of Judah with green, gold, and red. [alce::row_0972::p59]
> There is no central authority controlling the movement and significant variation exists among practitioners. [alce::row_0972::p59]
> Some Rastafarians see Rasta more as a way of life than a religion. [alce::row_0972::p5]
> Bob Marley is the most famous Rastafari, and his reggae music gained the Jamaican movement international recognition. [alce::row_0972::p5]
> The term "Rastafarianism" is considered derogatory and offensive by some Rastas, who dislike being labeled as an "ism." [alce::row_0972::p50]

### `row_0978`
> # Differences Between IRA, Roth IRA, and 401(k)

**Sponsorship and Access:**
A 401(k) is sponsored by an employer, so if you're not working, you cannot have one. [alce::row_0978::p41]
> In contrast, Roth IRAs are started between an investment firm and individuals who come to them. [alce::row_0978::p0]
> **Control of Funds:**
With a 401(k), you have no say in how the funds are controlled, and it is the sole prerogative of the employer to invest the funds. [alce::row_0978::p1]
> In a Roth IRA, you are in better control of the funds. [alce::row_0978::p1]
> **Tax Timing:**
A critical difference between these accounts boils down to whether a person wants to pay taxes now or when they retire. [alce::row_0978::p1]
> **How Contributions Work:**
With a 401(k), workers permit their employers to put a percentage of their pay into the account.
> Roth IRAs operate differently, as they are individual accounts managed between the account holder and an investment firm rather than through an employer.

Cited: alce::row_0978::p0, alce::row_0978::p1, alce::row_0978::p41

### `row_0979`
> Time appears to pass slowly when we work and fast when we don't due to differences in brain activity and engagement. When someone enters a flow state during engaging work, the brain's frontal cortex—which is responsible for our sense of time—becomes less active, causing subjects to report time passing either very fast or very slowly. [alce::row_0979::p81]
> Additionally, when you are busy with the "right stuff" that engages you, time goes by really fast, but when you are busy with the "wrong stuff," time seems to crawl on so slowly. [alce::row_0979::p56]
> Conversely, when waiting or in situations where you are not engaged, time passes more slowly because you are focused on the passage of time itself rather than being absorbed in an activity. [alce::row_0979::p78]

> The standard course of preparation for A-level exams is two years, though individual training programmes can be created if necessary. [alce::row_0982::p47]
> Students sit all A-level exams at the end of two years of study, rather than taking modular exams throughout the course as in previous years. [alce::row_0982::p92]
> Most courses are assessed entirely through exams, with reduced levels of coursework. [alce::row_0982::p92]
> Resits are available, but students must wait until May/June for a chance to improve their grades, as January exams have been scrapped. [alce::row_0982::p92]
> A-level exams differ from AS-level (Advanced Subsidiary) exams, which cover the first year of the two-year A-level curriculum and count for one credit, while A-level exams count for two credits. [alce::row_0982::p9]
> AS-level results no longer count towards A-level grades. [alce::row_0982::p92]
> The exam process is regulated by the British Pearson Edexcel examination board and requires compliance with established protocols, including oversight by British inspectors who monitor the entire process from receipt of exam materials through administration. [alce::row_0982::p66]

### `row_0987`
> # The Bee Dance: What It Is and How It Works

The dance bees perform is called the "waggle dance," which is shaped like a figure-eight or coffee bean pattern. [alce::row_0987::p14]
> The bee performs this dance on a vertical surface inside the hive. [alce::row_0987::p26]
> The dance encodes specific directional information through the orientation of the movements. Dancing straight up means to fly in the direction of the sun, straight down means away from the sun, and left and right mean to fly to the left or right relative to the sun. [alce::row_0987::p26]
> The dance contains all the information other bees need to locate the food source, including the distance from the hive, the direction, and the productivity of the food source. [alce::row_0987::p30]
> Other bees are able to interpret this information by observing the dance movements and extracting the encoded details about inclination, direction, distance, and other characteristics of the food source. [alce::row_0987::p1]

Cited: alce::row_0987::p1, alce::row_0987::p14, alce::row_0987::p26, alce::row_0987::p30

### `row_0992`
> Films are shown at around 24 fps (not 23 fps) because this frame rate was selected as the lowest speed at which sound could be embedded in film while still delivering a quality visual experience and saving on expensive film stock. [alce::row_0992::p49]

> Many theaters had previously shown silent films at 22 to 26 fps, so 24 fps was chosen as a standardized rate for sound film. [alce::row_0992::p0]
> This 24 fps standard became established for 35 mm sound film around 1930. [alce::row_0992::p0]

### `row_0996`
> # Secularism and Humanism: Key Differences

Secular humanism is a philosophy or life stance that embraces human reason. [alce::row_0996::p2]
> The two movements—secular humanism and religious humanism—are distinct both conceptually and historically. [alce::row_0996::p85]
> A key difference between secular humanist morality and religious morality is that secular humanist morality comes from society's moral consensus rather than from books written by old societies with outdated morality. [alce::row_0996::p12]
> Secular humanism tends to eschew any of the "trappings" of religion, including most ritual or ceremony. [alce::row_0996::p85]
> Secular humanism claims to rely on the reality of scientific facts, whereas religion operates differently in its basis for claims.
> Despite their similarities in motivations to action, the main difference is that secular humanism emphasizes scientific facts and reasoning, while religion relies on different foundational principles.

Cited: alce::row_0996::p12, alce::row_0996::p2, alce::row_0996::p85

### `row_0999`
